**Israel**,[^7] officially the **State of Israel**,[^8] is a country in the [Southern Levant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Levant "Southern Levant") region of [West Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Asia "West Asia"). It is [bordered](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Borders_of_Israel "Borders of Israel") by [Lebanon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanon "Lebanon") to the north, [Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria "Syria") to the northeast, [Jordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan "Jordan") to the east, and [Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt "Egypt") to the southwest. [Israel's western coast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_coastal_plain "Israeli coastal plain") lies on the [Mediterranean Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea "Mediterranean Sea"), its southern tip reaches the [Red Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Sea "Red Sea"), and to the east is [Earth's lowest point](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extremes_on_Earth "Extremes on Earth") near the [Dead Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dead_Sea "Dead Sea"). [Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem "Jerusalem") is the government seat and [proclaimed capital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Status_of_Jerusalem "Status of Jerusalem"),[^31] while [Tel Aviv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv "Tel Aviv") is Israel's [largest urban area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gush_Dan "Gush Dan") and [economic centre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_Israel "Economy of Israel").

The [Land of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_of_Israel "Land of Israel"), also called [Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestine_\(region\) "Palestine (region)") or the [Holy Land](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Land "Holy Land"), was home to the ancient [Canaanites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canaan "Canaan") and later the kingdoms of [Israel and Judah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Israel_and_Judah "Ancient Israel and Judah") and [Hasmonean Judea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hasmonean_Judea "Hasmonean Judea"). Located near [continental crossroads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levantine_corridor "Levantine corridor"), its [demographics shifted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demographic_history_of_Palestine_\(region\) "Demographic history of Palestine (region)") under various empires. 19th-century [European antisemitism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_antisemitism "European antisemitism") fuelled the [Zionist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionist "Zionist") movement for a [Jewish homeland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_homeland "Jewish homeland"), which gained [British](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire "British Empire") support with the 1917 [Balfour Declaration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration "Balfour Declaration"). After [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I"), Britain occupied the region and established [Mandatory Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine "Mandatory Palestine"). British rule and [Jewish immigration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aliyah "Aliyah") in the leadup to the [Holocaust](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Holocaust "The Holocaust") intensified [Arab-Jewish tensions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intercommunal_conflict_in_Mandatory_Palestine "Intercommunal conflict in Mandatory Palestine"),[^32] [^33] which escalated into [a civil war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1947%E2%80%931948_civil_war_in_Mandatory_Palestine "1947–1948 civil war in Mandatory Palestine") after the 1947 [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations") (UN) [Partition Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine "United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine").

Israel [declared independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Declaration_of_Independence "Israeli Declaration of Independence") as the [British Mandate ended](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/End_of_the_British_Mandate_for_Palestine "End of the British Mandate for Palestine") on 14 May 1948, followed by an [invasion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War "1948 Arab–Israeli War") by [Arab states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_world "Arab world"). The [1949 armistice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1949_Armistice_Agreements "1949 Armistice Agreements") expanded Israel beyond the UN plan,[^34] while no new Arab state was created, leaving [Gaza under Egyptian control](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Gaza_Strip_by_the_United_Arab_Republic "Occupation of the Gaza Strip by the United Arab Republic") and the [West Bank ruled by Jordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordanian_annexation_of_the_West_Bank "Jordanian annexation of the West Bank").[^34] [^35] [^36] Most [Palestinian Arabs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinians "Palestinians") [fled or were expelled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Palestinian_expulsion_and_flight "1948 Palestinian expulsion and flight") during the [Nakba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nakba "Nakba"),[^37] [^38] [^39] while Israeli independence prompted [antisemitism in the Arab world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitism_in_the_Arab_world "Antisemitism in the Arab world") and [Jewish exodus therefrom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_exodus_from_the_Muslim_world "Jewish exodus from the Muslim world"), mainly to Israel.[^40] [^41] After the 1967 [Six-Day War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Six-Day_War "Six-Day War"), Israel occupied the West Bank, Gaza and Egyptian [Sinai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_occupation_of_the_Sinai_Peninsula "Israeli occupation of the Sinai Peninsula"), and annexed [East Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_annexation_of_East_Jerusalem "Israeli annexation of East Jerusalem") and the Syrian [Golan Heights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golan_Heights_Law "Golan Heights Law"). Peace treaties were signed with [Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt%E2%80%93Israel_peace_treaty "Egypt–Israel peace treaty") in 1979 (the Sinai being returned in 1982) and [Jordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Jordan_peace_treaty "Israel–Jordan peace treaty") in 1994. The 1993 [Oslo Accords](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oslo_Accords "Oslo Accords") introduced limited [Palestinian self-rule](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_Authority "Palestinian Authority") in the West Bank and Gaza, while the 2020 [Abraham Accords](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_Accords "Abraham Accords") [normalised](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_normalization "Arab–Israeli normalization") ties with more Arab states, but the [Israeli–Palestinian conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict "Israeli–Palestinian conflict") persists. Israeli [occupation of the Palestinian territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli-occupied_territories "Israeli-occupied territories") has drawn international criticism, with experts calling its actions [war crimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_war_crimes "Israeli war crimes") and crimes against humanity. After the [Hamas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamas "Hamas") -led [October 7 attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_7_attacks "October 7 attacks"), Israel began committing [genocide against Palestinians in Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_genocide "Gaza genocide").[^42] Israel and its allies, including the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States"), [deny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_genocide_denial "Gaza genocide denial") that Israel's actions constitute genocide.[^43] [^44] [^45]

The [Basic Laws of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basic_Laws_of_Israel "Basic Laws of Israel") establish the [Knesset](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knesset "Knesset") as a [proportionally](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proportional_representation "Proportional representation") elected [parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_system "Parliamentary system"). It shapes the [government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_of_Israel "Cabinet of Israel"), led by the [prime minister](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Israel "Prime Minister of Israel"), and elects the largely ceremonial [president](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_Israel "President of Israel").[^46] Israel has one of the Middle East's largest economies,[^47] [one of Asia's highest living standards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_in_Asia_and_Oceania_by_Human_Development_Index "List of countries in Asia and Oceania by Human Development Index"), and globally ranks [25th in nominal GDP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_\(nominal\) "List of countries by GDP (nominal)") and [14th in nominal GDP per capita](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_\(nominal\)_per_capita "List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita").[^28] [^48] One of the world's most [technologically advanced](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Israel "Science and technology in Israel") countries,[^49] Israel allocates a larger share of its economy to research and development [than any other state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_by_research_and_development_spending "List of sovereign states by research and development spending") [^50] [^51] and is believed to [possess nuclear weapons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_and_nuclear_weapons "Israel and nuclear weapons"). The only country with a [revived](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revival_of_the_Hebrew_language "Revival of the Hebrew language") official language, [Hebrew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_Hebrew "Modern Hebrew"), the [culture of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_of_Israel "Culture of Israel") combines [Jewish traditions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_culture "Jewish culture") with [Arab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_culture "Arab culture") influences.

## Etymology

The names [Land of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_of_Israel "Land of Israel") and Children of Israel have historically been used to refer to the biblical [Kingdom of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_\(united_monarchy\) "Kingdom of Israel (united monarchy)") and the entire [Jewish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jews "Jews") people respectively. The [name *Israel*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_\(name\) "Israel (name)") (Hebrew: *Yīsrāʾēl*; [Septuagint](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Septuagint "Septuagint") [Ancient Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language "Ancient Greek language"): Ἰσραήλ, *Israēl*, " [El (God)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_\(deity\) "El (deity)") persists/rules") refers to the patriarch [Jacob](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacob "Jacob") who, according to the [Hebrew Bible](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_Bible "Hebrew Bible"), was given the name after he successfully [wrestled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacob_wrestling_with_the_angel "Jacob wrestling with the angel") with the [Angel of the Lord](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angel_of_the_Lord "Angel of the Lord").[^52] The earliest known archaeological artefact to mention the word *Israel* as a collective is the [Merneptah Stele](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Merneptah_Stele "Merneptah Stele") of [ancient Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Egypt "Ancient Egypt") (dated to the late-13th century BCE).[^53] [^54] [^55] [^6] [^57]

Under the [British Mandate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandate_for_Palestine "Mandate for Palestine") (1920–1948), the entire region was known as *Palestine*.[^58] [^59] Upon [establishment in 1948](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Declaration_of_Independence "Israeli Declaration of Independence"), the country formally adopted the name *State of Israel* ([Hebrew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_language "Hebrew language"): מְדִינַת יִשְׂרָאֵל, [**Medīnat Yisrā'el**](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/9/93/He-Medinat_Israel.ogg/He-Medinat_Israel.ogg.mp3 "Play audio") [\[mediˈnat jisʁaˈʔel\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Hebrew "Help:IPA/Hebrew"); [Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language "Arabic language"): دَوْلَة إِسْرَائِيل, **Dawlat Isrāʼīl**, [\[dawlat ʔisraːˈʔiːl\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Arabic "Help:IPA/Arabic")) after other [proposed names](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Declaration_of_Independence#Name "Israeli Declaration of Independence") including *[Land of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_of_Israel "Land of Israel")* (*Eretz Israel*), *Ever* (from ancestor [Eber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eber "Eber")), *[Zion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zion "Zion")*, and *[Judea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judea "Judea")*, were considered but rejected.[^60] [^61] The name *Israel* was suggested by [David Ben-Gurion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion "David Ben-Gurion") and passed by a vote of 6–3.[^62] [^63] In the early weeks after establishment, the government chose the term *[Israeli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israelis "Israelis")* to denote a citizen of the state.[^64]

## History

### Prehistory

The [Ubeidiya prehistoric site](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ubeidiya_prehistoric_site "Ubeidiya prehistoric site") in northern Israel shows the [presence of archaic humans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_expansions_of_hominins_out_of_Africa "Early expansions of hominins out of Africa") around 1.5 million years ago.[^65] The second-oldest evidence of [anatomically modern humans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatomically_modern_human "Anatomically modern human") [outside Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recent_African_origin_of_modern_humans "Recent African origin of modern humans") is a 200,000-year-old fossil from [Misliya Cave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Misliya_Cave "Misliya Cave") on Mount Carmel.[^66] The [Natufian culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natufian_culture "Natufian culture") (c. 10,000 BCE) may be linked to the [Proto-Afroasiatic language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Afroasiatic_language "Proto-Afroasiatic language") [^67] [^68] and is notable for adopting [sedentism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sedentism "Sedentism") before the [advent of agriculture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Origins_of_agriculture_in_West_Asia "Origins of agriculture in West Asia") and the [Neolithic Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution "Neolithic Revolution").[^69]

### Bronze and Iron Ages

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ruins_atop_Tel_Megiddo_with_circular_altar-like_shrine_and_a_series_of_temples_on_top_of_the_other_dating_from_the_early_bronze-age_through_the_iron-age_periods%2C_Tel_Meggido%2C_Israel_%2819888642855%29.jpg/250px-thumbnail.jpg)

Tel Megiddo, the ruins of a Canaanite and later Israelite city

Early references to " [Canaan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canaan "Canaan") " and "Canaanites" appear in ancient [Near Eastern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Near_East "Ancient Near East") and [Egyptian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Egypt "Ancient Egypt") texts (c. 2000 BCE); these populations were structured as politically independent [city-states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/City-state "City-state").[^70] [^71] During the [Late Bronze Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Bronze_Age "Late Bronze Age") (1550–1200 BCE), large parts of Canaan formed [vassal states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vassal_state "Vassal state") of the [New Kingdom of Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Kingdom_of_Egypt "New Kingdom of Egypt").[^72] As a result of the [Late Bronze Age collapse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Bronze_Age_collapse "Late Bronze Age collapse"), Canaan fell into chaos, and Egyptian control over the region collapsed.[^73] [^74] Ancestors of the [Israelites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israelites "Israelites") are thought to have included [ancient Semitic-speaking peoples](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Semitic-speaking_peoples "Ancient Semitic-speaking peoples") native to this area.[^75]<sup><span title="Page / location: 78–79">: 78–79</span> </sup> Modern archaeological accounts suggest that the Israelites and their culture branched out of the Canaanite peoples through the development of a distinct [monolatristic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monolatry "Monolatry") —and later [monotheistic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monotheism "Monotheism") —religion centered on [Yahweh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yahweh "Yahweh").[^76] [^77] They spoke an archaic form of [Hebrew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_language "Hebrew language"), known as [Biblical Hebrew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biblical_Hebrew "Biblical Hebrew").[^78] Around the same time, the [Philistines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philistines "Philistines") settled on the southern [coastal plain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_coastal_plain "Israeli coastal plain").[^79] [^80]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Mesad_Hashavyahu_ostracon.jpg/250px-Mesad_Hashavyahu_ostracon.jpg)

The Yavne-Yam ostracon, a Paleo-Hebrew inscription documenting administration in Judah

Most modern scholars agree that the [Exodus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Exodus "The Exodus") narrative in the [Torah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Torah "Torah") and [Old Testament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Testament "Old Testament") did not take place as depicted; however, some elements of these traditions do have [historical roots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historicity_of_the_Bible "Historicity of the Bible").[^81] [^82] There is debate about the earliest existence of the [Kingdoms of Israel and Judah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_ancient_Israel_and_Judah "History of ancient Israel and Judah") and their extent and power. While it is unclear if there was a [United Kingdom of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_\(united_monarchy\) "Kingdom of Israel (united monarchy)"),[^83] [^84] historians and archaeologists agree that the northern [Kingdom of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_\(Samaria\) "Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)") existed by ca. 900 BCE [^85]<sup><span title="Page / location: 169–195">: 169–195</span> </sup> and the [Kingdom of Judah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Judah "Kingdom of Judah") by ca. 850 BCE.[^86] [^87] The Kingdom of Israel was the more prosperous of the two and soon developed into a regional power, with a capital at [Samaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samaria_\(ancient_city\) "Samaria (ancient city)");[^88] [^89] [^90] during the [Omride dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omrides "Omrides"), it controlled [Samaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samaria "Samaria"), [Galilee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galilee "Galilee"), the upper [Jordan Valley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan_Valley "Jordan Valley"), the [plain of Sharon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharon_plain "Sharon plain") and large parts of [Transjordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transjordan_\(region\) "Transjordan (region)").[^89] The Kingdom of Israel [was conquered](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samerina "Samerina") around 720 BCE by the [Neo-Assyrian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Assyrian_Empire "Neo-Assyrian Empire").[^91] The Kingdom of Judah, under [Davidic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Davidic_line "Davidic line") rule with its capital in [Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem "Jerusalem"), later became a [client state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Client_state "Client state") of first the Neo-Assyrian Empire and then the [Neo-Babylonian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Babylonian_Empire "Neo-Babylonian Empire"). It is estimated that [the region's population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demographic_history_of_Palestine_\(region\) "Demographic history of Palestine (region)") was around 400,000 in the [Iron Age II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron_Age_II "Iron Age II").[^92] In 587/6 BCE, following a [revolt in Judah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judah%27s_revolts_against_Babylon "Judah's revolts against Babylon"), King [Nebuchadnezzar II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nebuchadnezzar_II "Nebuchadnezzar II") [besieged and destroyed Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_\(587_BC\) "Siege of Jerusalem (587 BC)") and [Solomon's Temple](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solomon%27s_Temple "Solomon's Temple"),[^93] [^94] dissolved the kingdom and [exiled much of the Judean elite to Babylon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylonian_captivity "Babylonian captivity").[^95]

### Classical antiquity

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Monnaie_-_Prutah%2C_bronze%2C_J%C3%A9rusalem%2C_Jud%C3%A9e%2C_Mattathias_Antigonos_-_btv1b8480202s_%281_of_2%29.jpg/250px-Monnaie_-_Prutah%2C_bronze%2C_J%C3%A9rusalem%2C_Jud%C3%A9e%2C_Mattathias_Antigonos_-_btv1b8480202s_%281_of_2%29.jpg)

Hasmonean coin of Antigonus II Mattathias, depicting the Temple menorah

After [capturing Babylon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_Babylon "Fall of Babylon") in 539 BCE, [Cyrus the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyrus_the_Great "Cyrus the Great"), founder of the [Achaemenid Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire "Achaemenid Empire"), issued [a proclamation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edict_of_Cyrus "Edict of Cyrus") allowing the exiled Judean population to return.[^96] [^97] The construction of the [Second Temple](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Temple "Second Temple") was completed c. 520 BCE.[^96] The Achaemenids ruled the region as the province of [Yehud Medinata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yehud_Medinata "Yehud Medinata").[^98] In 332 BCE, [Alexander the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_the_Great "Alexander the Great") conquered the region as part of his [campaign against the Achaemenid Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wars_of_Alexander_the_Great "Wars of Alexander the Great"). After his death, the area [was controlled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenistic_Palestine "Hellenistic Palestine") by the [Ptolemaic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ptolemaic_Kingdom "Ptolemaic Kingdom") and [Seleucid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seleucid_Empire "Seleucid Empire") empires as a part of [Coele-Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coele-Syria "Coele-Syria"). Under the Hellenistic kingdoms, ongoing [Hellenisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenization "Hellenization") generated cultural tensions among the Jewish population that culminated under [Antiochus IV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antiochus_IV_Epiphanes "Antiochus IV Epiphanes"), whose decrees outlawed Jewish practices and triggered the [Maccabean Revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maccabean_Revolt "Maccabean Revolt") in 167 BCE. The revolt weakened Seleucid control over Judea; by 142/141 BCE the [Hasmoneans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hasmonean_dynasty "Hasmonean dynasty") had secured autonomy and soon established an [independent Jewish kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hasmonean_Judea "Hasmonean Judea") that, in the late 2nd–early 1st century BCE, expanded into neighbouring territories.[^99] [^100] [^101] The [Hasmonean civil war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hasmonean_civil_war "Hasmonean civil war") ended with the [Roman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Republic "Roman Republic") [siege of Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_\(63_BC\) "Siege of Jerusalem (63 BC)") in 63 BCE.

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Israel-2013-Aerial_21-Masada.jpg/250px-Israel-2013-Aerial_21-Masada.jpg)

View of the Masada fortress overlooking the Dead Sea, which is the location of a 1st-century Roman siege

In 37 BCE, [Herod the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herod_the_Great "Herod the Great") was installed as a [dynastic vassal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herodian_dynasty "Herodian dynasty") of [Rome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Rome "Ancient Rome") following the [Roman–Parthian Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman%E2%80%93Parthian_Wars "Roman–Parthian Wars"). In 6 CE, the area was annexed as the [Roman province of Judaea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaea_\(Roman_province\) "Judaea (Roman province)"); tensions with Roman rule led to a series of [Jewish–Roman wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish%E2%80%93Roman_wars "Jewish–Roman wars"), resulting in widespread destruction. The [First Jewish–Roman War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Jewish%E2%80%93Roman_War "First Jewish–Roman War") (66–73 CE) resulted in the [destruction of Jerusalem and the Second Temple](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_\(70_CE\) "Siege of Jerusalem (70 CE)") and a sizable portion of the population being killed or displaced.[^102] A second uprising known as the [Bar Kokhba revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_Kokhba_revolt "Bar Kokhba revolt") (132–136 CE) initially allowed the Jews to form an independent state, but the Romans brutally crushed the rebellion, devastating and depopulating Judea's countryside.[^102] [^103] [^104] [^105] [^106] Jerusalem was rebuilt as a [Roman colony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonia_\(Roman\) "Colonia (Roman)") ([Aelia Capitolina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aelia_Capitolina "Aelia Capitolina")), and the province of Judea was renamed [Syria Palaestina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria_Palaestina "Syria Palaestina").[^107] [^108] Jews were expelled from the districts surrounding Jerusalem.[^105] [^109] Nevertheless, there was a continuous small Jewish presence, and Galilee became its religious center.[^110] [^111]

### Late antiquity and the medieval period

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Ruins_of_the_Ancient_Synagogue_at_Bar%27am.jpg/250px-Ruins_of_the_Ancient_Synagogue_at_Bar%27am.jpg)

3rd-century Kfar Bar'am synagogue in the Galilee 112

During the [Byzantine period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Palestine "Byzantine Palestine"), [Early Christianity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_Christianity "Early Christianity") displaced [Roman paganism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_in_ancient_Rome "Religion in ancient Rome") in the 4th century CE, with [Constantine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantine_the_Great "Constantine the Great") embracing and promoting the Christian religion and [Theodosius I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theodosius_I "Theodosius I") making it [the state religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity_as_the_Roman_state_religion "Christianity as the Roman state religion"). A series of laws were passed that discriminated against Jews and Judaism, and Jews were persecuted by both the church and the authorities.[^113] Many Jews had emigrated to flourishing [diaspora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_diaspora "Jewish diaspora") communities,[^114] while locally there was both Christian immigration and local conversion. By the middle of the 5th century, there was a Christian majority.[^115] [^116] Towards the end of the 5th century, [Samaritan revolts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samaritan_revolts "Samaritan revolts") erupted, continuing until the late 6th century and resulting in a large decrease in the Samaritan population.[^117] After the [Sasanian conquest of Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sasanian_conquest_of_Jerusalem "Sasanian conquest of Jerusalem") and the short-lived [Jewish revolt against Heraclius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_revolt_against_Heraclius "Jewish revolt against Heraclius") in 614 CE, the Byzantine Empire [reconsolidated control of the area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine%E2%80%93Sasanian_War_of_602%E2%80%93628 "Byzantine–Sasanian War of 602–628") in 628.[^118]

In 634–641 CE, the [Rashidun Caliphate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate "Rashidun Caliphate") [conquered the Levant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Levant "Muslim conquest of the Levant").[^114] [^119] [^120] Caliph [Umar ibn al-Khattab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umar_ibn_al-Khattab "Umar ibn al-Khattab") (r. 634–644) lifted the Christian ban on Jews entering [Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem "Jerusalem") and permitted them to worship there.[^121] Over the next six centuries, control of the region transferred between the [Umayyad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate "Umayyad Caliphate"), [Abbasid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate "Abbasid Caliphate"), and [Fatimid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate "Fatimid Caliphate") caliphates, and subsequently the [Seljuk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seljuk_dynasty "Seljuk dynasty") and [Ayyubid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ayyubid_dynasty "Ayyubid dynasty") dynasties.[^122] The population drastically decreased during the following several centuries, dropping from an estimated 1 million during Roman and Byzantine periods to about 300,000 by the early [Ottoman period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire"), and there was steady [Arabisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabization "Arabization") and [Islamisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamization "Islamization").[^123] [^92] [^119] [^120] [^124] The end of the 11th century brought the [Crusades](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crusades "Crusades"), [papally](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope "Pope") -sanctioned incursions of Christian crusaders intent on wresting Jerusalem and the [Holy Land](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Land "Holy Land") from Muslim control and establishing [crusader states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crusader_states "Crusader states").[^125] The Ayyubids pushed back the crusaders before Muslim rule was fully restored by the [Mamluk sultans of Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate_\(Cairo\) "Mamluk Sultanate (Cairo)") in 1291.[^126]

### Modern period and the emergence of Zionism

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Jews_at_Western_Wall_by_Felix_Bonfils%2C_1870s.jpg/250px-Jews_at_Western_Wall_by_Felix_Bonfils%2C_1870s.jpg)

Jews at the Western Wall in the 1870s, a holy site in Judaism

In 1516, the Ottoman Empire conquered the region and ruled it as part of [Ottoman Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Syria "Ottoman Syria").[^127] [^123] Two violent incidents took place against Jews, the [1517 Safed attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1517_Safed_attacks "1517 Safed attacks") and the [1517 Hebron attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1517_Hebron_attacks "1517 Hebron attacks"), after the Turkish Ottomans ousted the [Mamluks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mamluk "Mamluk") during the [Ottoman–Mamluk War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Mamluk_War_\(1516%E2%80%931517\) "Ottoman–Mamluk War (1516–1517)").[^128] [^129] Under the Ottoman Empire, the Levant was fairly cosmopolitan, with religious freedoms for [Christians, Muslims, and Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People_of_the_Book "People of the Book"). In 1561 the [Ottoman sultan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent "Suleiman the Magnificent") invited [Sephardic Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sephardic_Jews "Sephardic Jews") escaping the [Spanish Inquisition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition "Spanish Inquisition") to settle in and rebuild the city of [Tiberias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tiberias "Tiberias").[^130] [^131]

Under the Ottoman Empire's [millet system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Millet_\(Ottoman_Empire\) "Millet (Ottoman Empire)"), Christians and Jews were considered *[dhimmi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dhimmi "Dhimmi")* ("protected") under [Ottoman law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_law "Ottoman law") in exchange for loyalty to the state and payment of the *[jizya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jizya "Jizya")* tax.[^132] [^133] Non-Muslim Ottoman subjects faced geographic and lifestyle restrictions, though these were not always enforced.[^134] [^135] [^136] The millet system organised non-Muslims into autonomous communities on the basis of religion.[^137]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/THEODOR_HERZL_AT_THE_FIRST_ZIONIST_CONGRESS_IN_BASEL_ON_25.8.1897._%D7%AA%D7%90%D7%95%D7%93%D7%95%D7%A8_%D7%94%D7%A8%D7%A6%D7%9C_%D7%91%D7%A7%D7%95%D7%A0%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%A1_%D7%94%D7%A6%D7%99%D7%95%D7%A0%D7%99_%D7%94%D7%A8%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%95%D7%9F_-_1897.8.25.jpg/250px-THEODOR_HERZL_AT_THE_FIRST_ZIONIST_CONGRESS_IN_BASEL_ON_25.8.1897._%D7%AA%D7%90%D7%95%D7%93%D7%95%D7%A8_%D7%94%D7%A8%D7%A6%D7%9C_%D7%91%D7%A7%D7%95%D7%A0%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%A1_%D7%94%D7%A6%D7%99%D7%95%D7%A0%D7%99_%D7%94%D7%A8%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%95%D7%9F_-_1897.8.25.jpg)

The First Zionist Congress (1897) in Basel, Switzerland

The [concept of an eventual return to Zion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Return_to_Zion "Return to Zion") remained a symbol within religious Jewish belief which emphasised that their return should be determined by [Divine Providence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Divine_providence_in_Judaism "Divine providence in Judaism") rather than human action.[^138] The Jewish population of Palestine from the Ottoman rule to the beginning of the Zionist movement, known as the [Old Yishuv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Yishuv "Old Yishuv"), comprised a minority and fluctuated in size. During the 16th century, Jewish communities struck roots in the [Four Holy Cities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Four_Holy_Cities "Four Holy Cities") —Jerusalem, Tiberias, [Hebron](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebron "Hebron"), and [Safed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safed "Safed") —and in 1697, Rabbi Yehuda Hachasid led 1,500 Jews to Jerusalem.[^139] A 1660 [Druze revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Druze_power_struggle_\(1658%E2%80%931667\)#Lebanon_and_Galilee_campaign "Druze power struggle (1658–1667)") against the Ottomans destroyed [Safed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1660_destruction_of_Safed "1660 destruction of Safed") and [Tiberias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1660_destruction_of_Tiberias "1660 destruction of Tiberias").[^127] In the second half of the 18th century, Eastern European Jews who were [opponents](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Misnagdim "Misnagdim") of [Hasidism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hasidic_Judaism "Hasidic Judaism"), known as the [Perushim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perushim "Perushim"), settled in Palestine.[^140] [^141]

In the late 18th century, local Arab Sheikh [Daher al-Umar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daher_al-Umar "Daher al-Umar") created a de facto independent emirate in the Galilee. Ottoman attempts to subdue the sheikh failed. After Daher's death the Ottomans regained control of the area. In 1799, governor [Jazzar Pasha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jazzar_Pasha "Jazzar Pasha") repelled an [assault on Acre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Acre_\(1799\) "Siege of Acre (1799)") by [Napoleon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleon "Napoleon") 's troops, prompting the French to abandon the Syrian campaign.[^142] In 1834, a [revolt by Palestinian Arab peasants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peasants%27_revolt_in_Palestine "Peasants' revolt in Palestine") against Egyptian conscription and taxation policies under [Muhammad Ali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_of_Egypt "Muhammad Ali of Egypt") was suppressed; Muhammad Ali's army retreated and Ottoman rule was restored with British support in 1840.[^143] The [Tanzimat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanzimat "Tanzimat") reforms were implemented across the Ottoman Empire.

The first wave of modern Jewish migration to [Ottoman-ruled Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Syria "Southern Syria"), known as the [First Aliyah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Aliyah "First Aliyah"), began in 1881, as Jews fled [pogroms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pogrom "Pogrom") in Eastern Europe.[^144] The 1882 [May Laws](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/May_Laws "May Laws") increased economic discrimination against Jews, and restricted where they could live.[^145] [^146] Antisemitism, pogroms and official policies in tsarist Russia led to the emigration of three million Jews in the years between 1882 and 1914, only 1% of whom went to Palestine. Those who went to Palestine were driven primarily by ideas of self-determination and Jewish identity, rather than as a response to pogroms or economic insecurity.[^138] [Zionism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionism "Zionism") emerged during this time as a political movement to reestablish a Jewish homeland in Palestine.[^147] The [revival of the Hebrew language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revival_of_the_Hebrew_language "Revival of the Hebrew language"), during which [Hebrew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_language "Hebrew language") was adapted for modern use and gradually became the primary language of Jews in Palestine, also began.[^148]

The [Second Aliyah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Aliyah "Second Aliyah") (1904–1914) began after the [Kishinev pogrom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kishinev_pogrom "Kishinev pogrom"); some 40,000 Jews settled in Palestine, although nearly half left eventually. Both the first and second waves of migrants were mainly [Orthodox Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orthodox_Judaism "Orthodox Judaism").[^149] The Second Aliyah included [Zionist socialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labor_Zionism "Labor Zionism") groups who established the *[kibbutz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kibbutz "Kibbutz")* movement based on the idea of establishing a separate Jewish economy based exclusively on Jewish labour.[^150] [^151] Those of the Second Aliyah who became leaders of the [Yishuv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yishuv "Yishuv") in the coming decades believed that the Jewish settler economy should not depend on Arab labour. This would be a dominant source of antagonism with the Arab population, with the new Yishuv's nationalist ideology overpowering its socialist one.[^152] Though the immigrants of the Second Aliyah largely sought to create communal Jewish agricultural settlements, [Tel Aviv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv "Tel Aviv") was established as the first planned Jewish town in 1909. Jewish armed militias emerged during this period, the first being [Bar-Giora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar-Giora_\(organization\) "Bar-Giora (organization)") in 1907. Two years later, the larger [Hashomer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hashomer "Hashomer") organisation was founded as its replacement.[^153]

### British Mandate for Palestine

[Chaim Weizmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chaim_Weizmann "Chaim Weizmann") 's efforts to garner British support for the Zionist movement eventually secured the [Balfour Declaration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration "Balfour Declaration") of 1917,[^154] stating Britain's support for the creation of a Jewish " [national home](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homeland_for_the_Jewish_people "Homeland for the Jewish people") " in Palestine.[^155] [^156] Weizmann's interpretation of the declaration was that negotiations on the future of the country were to happen directly between Britain and the Jews, excluding Arabs. [Jewish-Arab relations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic%E2%80%93Jewish_relations "Islamic–Jewish relations") in Palestine deteriorated dramatically in the following years.[^157]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Allenby_Street.JPG/250px-Allenby_Street.JPG)

Tel Aviv in the 1930s

In 1918, the [Jewish Legion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_Legion "Jewish Legion"), primarily Zionist volunteers, assisted in the British [conquest of Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinai_and_Palestine_campaign "Sinai and Palestine campaign").[^158] In 1920, the territory was divided between Britain and [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France "France") under the [mandate system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate "League of Nations mandate"), and the British-administered area (including modern Israel) was named [Mandatory Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine "Mandatory Palestine").[^126] [^159] [^160] Arab opposition to British rule and Jewish immigration led to the [1920 Palestine riots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1920_Nebi_Musa_riots "1920 Nebi Musa riots") and the formation of a Jewish militia known as the [Haganah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haganah "Haganah") as an outgrowth of Hashomer, from which the [Irgun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irgun "Irgun") and [Lehi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lehi_\(group\) "Lehi (group)") paramilitaries later split.[^161] In 1922, the [League of Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/League_of_Nations "League of Nations") granted Britain the [Mandate for Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandate_for_Palestine "Mandate for Palestine") under terms which included the Balfour Declaration with its promise to the Jews and with similar provisions regarding the Arab Palestinians.[^162] The [population of the area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demographic_history_of_Palestine_\(region\) "Demographic history of Palestine (region)") was predominantly Arab and Muslim, with Jews accounting for about 11% [^163] and Arab Christians about 9.5% of the population.[^164]

The [Third](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_Aliyah "Third Aliyah") (1919–1923) and [Fourth Aliyahs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fourth_Aliyah "Fourth Aliyah") (1924–1929) brought an additional 100,000 Jews to Palestine. The [rise of Nazism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler%27s_rise_to_power "Adolf Hitler's rise to power") and the increasing persecution of Jews in 1930s Europe led to the [Fifth Aliyah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fifth_Aliyah "Fifth Aliyah"), with an influx of a quarter of a million Jews. This was a major cause of the [Arab revolt of 1936–39](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine "1936–1939 Arab revolt in Palestine"), which was suppressed by British security forces and Zionist militias. Several hundred British security personnel and Jews were killed; 5,032 Arabs were killed, 14,760 wounded, and 12,622 detained.[^165] [^166] [^167] An estimated ten per cent of the adult male [Palestinian Arab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_people "Palestinian people") population was killed, wounded, imprisoned, or exiled.[^168]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/%22Jews_and_Arabs_in_Grim_Struggle_for_Holy_Land%22_article_%281938%29.jpg/250px-%22Jews_and_Arabs_in_Grim_Struggle_for_Holy_Land%22_article_%281938%29.jpg)

"Jews and Arabs in Grim Struggle for Holy Land", article from 1938

The British introduced restrictions on Jewish immigration to Palestine with the [White Paper of 1939](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Paper_of_1939 "White Paper of 1939"). With countries around the world turning away Jewish refugees fleeing [the Holocaust](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Holocaust "The Holocaust"), a clandestine movement known as [Aliyah Bet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aliyah_Bet "Aliyah Bet") was organised to bring Jews to Palestine. During [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II"), Palestine was [repeatedly bombed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_bombing_of_Mandatory_Palestine_in_World_War_II "Italian bombing of Mandatory Palestine in World War II") by Axis aircraft, causing casualties among both Jews and Arabs. About 30,000 Jews from Palestine served in the British military during the war, of whom around 700 were killed.[^169] Some 12,000 Palestinian Arabs also served in the British military during the war.[^170] At the end of the war, about 31% of the population of Palestine was Jewish.[^171] The UK found itself facing a [Jewish insurgency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_insurgency_in_Mandatory_Palestine "Jewish insurgency in Mandatory Palestine") over immigration restrictions from 1944, which intensified following the end of the war, and continued conflict with the Arab community over limit levels. The Haganah joined Irgun and Lehi in an armed struggle against British rule.[^172] The Haganah attempted to bring tens of thousands of Jewish refugees and [Holocaust survivors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust_survivors "Holocaust survivors") to Palestine by ship. Most of the ships were intercepted by the [Royal Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Navy "Royal Navy") and the refugees placed in detention camps in [Atlit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlit_detainee_camp "Atlit detainee camp") and [Cyprus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprus_internment_camps "Cyprus internment camps").[^173] [^174]

On 22 July 1946, Irgun [bombed the British administrative headquarters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_David_Hotel_bombing "King David Hotel bombing") for Palestine, killing 91.[^175] [^176] [^177] [^178] The attack was a response to [Operation Agatha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Agatha "Operation Agatha") (a series of raids, including one on the [Jewish Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_Agency_for_Israel "Jewish Agency for Israel"), by the British) and was the deadliest directed at the British during the Mandate era.[^177] [^178] The Jewish insurgency continued throughout 1946 and 1947 despite concerted efforts by the British military and [Palestine Police Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestine_Police_Force "Palestine Police Force") to suppress it.

British efforts to mediate with Jewish and Arab representatives were not successful as the Jews were unwilling to accept any solution that did not involve a Jewish state and suggested a partition of Palestine into Jewish and Arab states, while the Arabs were adamant that a Jewish state in any part of Palestine was unacceptable and that the only solution was a unified Palestine under Arab rule. In February 1947, the British referred the Palestine issue to the newly formed [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations"). On 15 May 1947, the [UN General Assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Assembly_of_the_United_Nations "General Assembly of the United Nations") resolved that a [Special Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Special_Committee_on_Palestine "United Nations Special Committee on Palestine") be created "to prepare... a report on the question of Palestine".[^179] The Report of the Committee [^180] [proposed a plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine "United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine") to replace the British Mandate with "an independent Arab State, an independent Jewish State, and the City of Jerusalem \[...\] the last to be under an International Trusteeship System".[^181]

Meanwhile, the Jewish insurgency continued and peaked in July 1947, with a series of widespread guerrilla raids culminating in [the Sergeants affair](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Sergeants_affair "The Sergeants affair"), in which the Irgun took two British sergeants hostage as attempted leverage against the planned execution of three Irgun operatives. After the executions were carried out, the Irgun killed the two British soldiers, hanged their bodies from trees, and left a booby trap at the scene which injured a British soldier. The incident caused widespread outrage in the UK.[^182] In September 1947, the British cabinet decided to evacuate Palestine as the Mandate was no longer tenable.[^183]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/UN_Palestine_Partition_Versions_1947.jpg/250px-UN_Palestine_Partition_Versions_1947.jpg)

1947 partition plan of Palestine between Israel and the State of Palestine, as proposed by the United Nations

On 29 November 1947, the General Assembly adopted [Resolution 181 (II)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine "United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine").[^184] The plan attached to the resolution was essentially that proposed in the report of 3 September. The Jewish Agency, the recognised representative of the Jewish community, accepted the plan, which assigned 55–56% of Mandatory Palestine to the Jews. At the time, the Jews were about a third of the population and owned around 6–7% of the land. Arabs constituted the majority and owned about 20% of the land, with the remainder held by the Mandate authorities or foreign landowners.[^185] [^186] [^187]

The [Arab League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_League "Arab League") and [Arab Higher Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Higher_Committee "Arab Higher Committee") of Palestine rejected the partition plan on the basis that the partition plan privileged European interests over those of the Palestinians,[^188] and indicated that they would reject any other plan of partition.[^189] [^190] On 1 December 1947, the Arab Higher Committee proclaimed a three-day strike, and [riots broke out in Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1947_Jerusalem_riots "1947 Jerusalem riots").[^191] The situation spiralled into [a civil war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1947%E2%80%931948_civil_war_in_Mandatory_Palestine "1947–1948 civil war in Mandatory Palestine"). Colonial Secretary [Arthur Creech Jones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Creech_Jones "Arthur Creech Jones") announced that the British Mandate would end on 15 May 1948, at which point the British would evacuate. As Arab militias and gangs attacked Jewish areas, they were faced mainly by the Haganah as well as the smaller Irgun and Lehi. In April 1948, the Haganah moved onto the offensive.[^192] [^193]

### Independence and early years

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948.jpg/250px-Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948.jpg)

David Ben-Gurion declaring the establishment of Israel on 14 May 1948

On 14 May 1948, the day before the expiration of the British Mandate, [David Ben-Gurion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion "David Ben-Gurion"), the head of the Jewish Agency, [declared "the establishment of a Jewish state in Eretz-Israel"](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Declaration_of_Independence "Israeli Declaration of Independence").[^194] The following day, the armies of four Arab countries—Egypt, Syria, Transjordan, and Iraq—entered what had been Mandatory Palestine, launching the [1948 Arab–Israeli War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War "1948 Arab–Israeli War");[^195] contingents from [Yemen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutawakkilite_Kingdom_of_Yemen "Mutawakkilite Kingdom of Yemen"), [Morocco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco "Morocco"), [Saudi Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia "Saudi Arabia"), and [Sudan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sudan "Sudan") joined the war.[^196] [^197] The purpose of the invasion was to prevent the establishment of the Jewish state.[^186] [^198] [^199] The Arab League stated the invasion was to restore order and prevent further bloodshed.[^200]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Raising_the_Ink_Flag_at_Umm_Rashrash_%28Eilat%29_%283x4%29.jpg/250px-Raising_the_Ink_Flag_at_Umm_Rashrash_%28Eilat%29_%283x4%29.jpg)

Raising of the Ink Flag on 10 March 1949, marking the end of the 1948 war

After a year of fighting, a [ceasefire was declared](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1949_Armistice_Agreements "1949 Armistice Agreements") and temporary borders, known as the [Green Line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_Line_\(Israel\) "Green Line (Israel)"), were established.[^201] [Jordan annexed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordanian_annexation_of_the_West_Bank "Jordanian annexation of the West Bank") what became known as the [West Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Bank "West Bank"), including [East Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Jerusalem "East Jerusalem"), and [Egypt occupied](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Gaza_Strip_by_the_United_Arab_Republic "Occupation of the Gaza Strip by the United Arab Republic") the [Gaza Strip](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_Strip "Gaza Strip"). Over 700,000 Palestinians [fled or were expelled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Palestinian_expulsion_and_flight "1948 Palestinian expulsion and flight") by [Zionist militias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionist_political_violence "Zionist political violence") and the [Israeli military](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_Defence_Forces "Israel Defence Forces") —what would become known in Arabic as the *[Nakba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nakba "Nakba")* ('catastrophe').[^202] The events also led to the destruction of most of Palestine's Arab [culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_of_Palestine "Culture of Palestine"), [identity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_identity "Palestinian identity"), and [national aspirations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_nationalism "Palestinian nationalism"). Some 156,000 Arabs remained and became [Arab citizens of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_citizens_of_Israel "Arab citizens of Israel").[^203]

By [United Nations General Assembly Resolution 273](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_273 "United Nations General Assembly Resolution 273"), Israel was admitted as a member of the UN on 11 May 1949.[^204] In the early years of the state, the [Labour Zionist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labor_Zionism "Labor Zionism") movement led by Prime Minister Ben-Gurion dominated [Israeli politics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politics_of_Israel "Politics of Israel").[^205] [^206] Immigration to Israel during the late 1940s and early 1950s was aided by the Israeli Immigration Department and the non-government sponsored [Mossad LeAliyah Bet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mossad_LeAliyah_Bet "Mossad LeAliyah Bet") (lit. "Institute for [Immigration B](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aliyah_Bet "Aliyah Bet") ").[^207] The latter engaged in clandestine operations in countries, particularly in the Middle East and Eastern Europe, where the lives of Jews were in danger and exit was difficult. Mossad LeAliyah Bet was disbanded in 1953.[^208] The immigration was in accordance with the [One Million Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One_Million_Plan "One Million Plan"). Some immigrants held Zionist beliefs or came for the promise of a better life, while others moved to escape persecution or were expelled from their homes.[^209] [^210]

An [influx of Holocaust survivors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aliyah#Early_statehood_\(1948%E2%80%931960\) "Aliyah") and [Jews from Arab and Muslim countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_exodus_from_the_Muslim_world "Jewish exodus from the Muslim world") to Israel during the first three years increased the number of Jews from 700,000 to 1,400,000. By 1958, the population had risen to two million.[^211] Between 1948 and 1970, approximately 1,150,000 Jewish refugees relocated to Israel.[^212] Some immigrants arrived as refugees and were housed in temporary camps known as *[ma'abarot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ma%27abarot "Ma'abarot")*; by 1952, over 200,000 people were living in these tent cities.[^213] [Jews of European background](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews "Ashkenazi Jews") were often treated more favourably than Jews from [Middle Eastern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mizrahi_Jews "Mizrahi Jews") and [North African](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sephardi_Jews "Sephardi Jews") countries—housing units reserved for the latter were often re-designated for the former, so Jews newly arrived from Arab lands generally ended up staying longer in transit camps.[^214] [^215] During this period, food, clothes and furniture were rationed in what became known as the [austerity period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austerity_in_Israel "Austerity in Israel"). The need to solve the crisis led Ben-Gurion to sign a [reparations agreement with West Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reparations_Agreement_between_Israel_and_the_Federal_Republic_of_Germany "Reparations Agreement between Israel and the Federal Republic of Germany") that triggered mass protests by Jews angered at the idea that Israel could accept monetary compensation for the Holocaust.[^216]

### Arab–Israeli conflict

There were [further expulsions of Palestinians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1949%E2%80%931956_Palestinian_expulsions "1949–1956 Palestinian expulsions") after the establishment of Israel. During the 1950s, Israel was [frequently attacked](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_attacks_against_Israeli_civilians_before_1967 "List of attacks against Israeli civilians before 1967") by [Palestinian fedayeen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_fedayeen "Palestinian fedayeen"), nearly always against civilians,[^217] mainly from the Egyptian-occupied Gaza Strip,[^218] leading to several Israeli [reprisal operations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reprisal_operations "Reprisal operations"). In 1956, the UK and France aimed at regaining control of the [Suez Canal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Canal "Suez Canal"), which Egypt had nationalised. The continued blockade of the Suez Canal and [Straits of Tiran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Straits_of_Tiran "Straits of Tiran") to Israeli shipping, together with increasing fedayeen attacks against Israel's southern population and recent Arab threatening statements, prompted Israel to attack Egypt.[^219] [^220] [^221] Israel joined [a secret alliance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protocol_of_S%C3%A8vres "Protocol of Sèvres") with the UK and France and overran the [Sinai Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula "Sinai Peninsula") in the [Suez Crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis "Suez Crisis") but was pressured to withdraw by the UN in return for guarantees of Israeli shipping rights.[^222] [^223] [^224] The war resulted in significant reduction of Israeli border infiltration.[^225]

1:14CC

U.S. newsreel on the trial of [Adolf Eichmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Eichmann "Adolf Eichmann")

In the early 1960s, Israel captured Nazi war criminal [Adolf Eichmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Eichmann "Adolf Eichmann") in Argentina and brought him to Israel [for trial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eichmann_trial "Eichmann trial").[^226] [^227] Eichmann remains the only person executed in Israel by conviction in an Israeli civilian court.[^228] In 1963, Israel was engaged in a diplomatic standoff with the United States in relation to the Israeli [nuclear programme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_and_Israel "Nuclear weapons and Israel").[^229] [^230]

Since 1964 Arab countries, concerned over Israeli plans to divert waters of the [Jordan River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan_River "Jordan River") into the [coastal plain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_coastal_plain "Israeli coastal plain"),[^231] had been trying to divert the headwaters to deprive Israel of water resources, [provoking tensions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_over_Water_\(Jordan_River\) "War over Water (Jordan River)") between Israel on the one hand, and Syria and Lebanon on the other. [Arab nationalists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_nationalist "Arab nationalist") led by Egyptian President [Gamal Abdel Nasser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser "Gamal Abdel Nasser") refused to recognise Israel and called for its destruction.[^232] [^233] [^234] By 1966, Israeli-Arab relations had deteriorated to the point of battles taking place between Israeli and Arab forces.[^235]

In May 1967, Egypt massed its army near the border with Israel, expelled [UN peacekeepers stationed in the Sinai Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Emergency_Force "United Nations Emergency Force") since 1957, and blocked Israel's access to the Red Sea.[^236] [^237] [^238] Other Arab states mobilised their forces.[^239] Israel reiterated that these actions were a *[casus belli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Casus_belli "Casus belli")* and launched a pre-emptive strike ([Operation Focus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Focus "Operation Focus")) against Egypt in June. Jordan, Syria and Iraq attacked Israel.

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Six_Day_War_Territories.svg/250px-Six_Day_War_Territories.svg.png)

Territory held by Israel: before the Six-Day War after the war The Sinai Peninsula was returned to Egypt in 1982.

In the ensuing [Six-Day War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Six-Day_War "Six-Day War"), Israel captured and occupied the West Bank from Jordan, the Gaza Strip and Sinai Peninsula from Egypt, and the Golan Heights from Syria.[^240] Israeli forces [expelled ~300,000 Palestinians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naksa "Naksa") from the Gaza Strip and the West Bank. Jerusalem's boundaries were enlarged, incorporating [East Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Jerusalem "East Jerusalem"). The 1949 Green Line became the administrative boundary between Israel and the [occupied territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli-occupied_territories "Israeli-occupied territories").[^241]

Following the 1967 war and the " [Three Nos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khartoum_Resolution "Khartoum Resolution") " resolution of the Arab League, Israel faced attacks from the Egyptians in the Sinai Peninsula during the 1967–1970 [War of Attrition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_of_Attrition "War of Attrition"), and from Palestinian groups targeting Israelis in the occupied territories, globally, and in Israel. Most important among the Palestinian and Arab groups was the [Palestine Liberation Organisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organisation "Palestine Liberation Organisation") (PLO), established in 1964, which initially committed itself to "armed struggle as the only way to liberate the homeland".[^242] In the late 1960s and early 1970s, [Palestinian groups launched attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_political_violence "Palestinian political violence") [^243] [^244] against Israeli and Jewish targets around the world,[^245] including [a massacre of Israeli athletes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Munich_massacre "Munich massacre") at the [1972 Summer Olympics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics "1972 Summer Olympics") in Munich. The Israeli government responded with an [assassination campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mossad_assassinations_following_the_Munich_massacre "Mossad assassinations following the Munich massacre") against the organisers of the massacre, [a bombing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1972_Israeli_air_raid_in_Syria_and_Lebanon "1972 Israeli air raid in Syria and Lebanon") and a [raid on the PLO headquarters in Lebanon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1973_Israeli_raid_in_Lebanon "1973 Israeli raid in Lebanon").

On 6 October 1973, the Egyptian and Syrian armies launched [a surprise attack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Badr_\(1973\) "Operation Badr (1973)") against Israeli forces in the Sinai Peninsula and Golan Heights, opening the [Yom Kippur War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War "Yom Kippur War"). The war ended on 25 October with Israel repelling Egyptian and Syrian forces but suffering great losses.[^246] An [internal inquiry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agranat_Commission "Agranat Commission") exonerated [the government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fifteenth_government_of_Israel "Fifteenth government of Israel") of responsibility for failures before and during the war, but public anger forced Prime Minister [Golda Meir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golda_Meir "Golda Meir") to resign.[^247] On 27 June 1976, [Air France Flight 139](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_France_Flight_139 "Air France Flight 139") was hijacked in flight from Israel to France by Palestinian guerrillas; Israeli commandos rescued 102 of 106 Israeli hostages days later.[^248]

### Peace process

The [1977 Knesset elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1977_Israeli_legislative_election "1977 Israeli legislative election") marked a major turning point in Israeli political history as [Menachem Begin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menachem_Begin "Menachem Begin") 's [Likud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Likud "Likud") party took control from the [Labor Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Labor_Party "Israeli Labor Party").[^249] Later that year, Egyptian President [Anwar El Sadat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anwar_El_Sadat "Anwar El Sadat") made a trip to Israel and spoke before the [Knesset](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knesset "Knesset") in what was the first recognition of Israel by an Arab head of state.[^250] Sadat and Begin signed the [Camp David Accords](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_David_Accords "Camp David Accords") (1978) and the [Egypt–Israel peace treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt%E2%80%93Israel_peace_treaty "Egypt–Israel peace treaty") (1979).[^251] In return, Israel withdrew from the Sinai Peninsula and agreed to enter negotiations over autonomy for Palestinians in the West Bank and the Gaza Strip.[^251]

On 11 March 1978, a PLO guerilla raid from Lebanon led to the [Coastal Road massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coastal_Road_massacre "Coastal Road massacre"). Israel responded by launching an [invasion of southern Lebanon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1978_South_Lebanon_conflict "1978 South Lebanon conflict") to destroy PLO bases. Begin's government meanwhile provided incentives for [Israelis to settle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_settlement "Israeli settlement") in the [occupied West Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_occupation_of_the_West_Bank "Israeli occupation of the West Bank"), increasing friction with the Palestinians there.[^252]

The 1980 [Jerusalem Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem_Law "Jerusalem Law") was believed by some to reaffirm Israel's 1967 annexation of Jerusalem by government decree and [reignited international controversy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UN_Security_Council_Resolution_478 "UN Security Council Resolution 478") over the [status of the city](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Status_of_Jerusalem "Status of Jerusalem"). No Israeli legislation has defined the territory of Israel, and no act specifically included East Jerusalem therein.[^253] In 1981 Israel [effectively annexed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golan_Heights_Law "Golan Heights Law") the Golan Heights.[^254] The international community largely rejected these moves, with the UN Security Council declaring both the Jerusalem Law and the Golan Heights Law null and void.[^255] [^256] Several waves of [Ethiopian Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beta_Israel "Beta Israel") [immigrated to Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aliyah_from_Ethiopia "Aliyah from Ethiopia") since the 1980s, while between 1990 and 1994, [immigration from the post-Soviet states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990s_post-Soviet_aliyah "1990s post-Soviet aliyah") increased Israel's population by twelve per cent.[^257]

On 7 June 1981, during the [Iran–Iraq War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War "Iran–Iraq War"), the [Israeli air force destroyed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Opera "Operation Opera") Iraq's sole nuclear reactor, then under construction, in order to impede the Iraqi nuclear weapons programme.[^258] Following a series of PLO attacks in 1982, Israel [invaded Lebanon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982_Lebanon_War "1982 Lebanon War") to destroy the PLO bases.[^259] In the first six days, Israel destroyed the military forces of the PLO in Lebanon and decisively defeated the Syrians. An Israeli government inquiry (the [Kahan Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kahan_Commission "Kahan Commission")) held Begin and several Israeli generals indirectly responsible for the [Sabra and Shatila massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sabra_and_Shatila_massacre "Sabra and Shatila massacre") and held [defence minister](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_\(Israel\) "Ministry of Defence (Israel)") [Ariel Sharon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ariel_Sharon "Ariel Sharon") as bearing "personal responsibility".[^260] Sharon was forced to resign.[^261]

In 1985, Israel responded to a Palestinian [terrorist attack in Cyprus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larnaca_yacht_killings "Larnaca yacht killings") by [bombing the PLO headquarters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Wooden_Leg "Operation Wooden Leg") in Tunisia. Israel withdrew from most of Lebanon in 1986 but continued to [occupy a borderland buffer zone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_occupation_of_Southern_Lebanon_\(1982%E2%80%932000\) "Israeli occupation of Southern Lebanon (1982–2000)") in southern Lebanon until 2000, from where Israeli forces [engaged in conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Lebanon_conflict_\(1985%E2%80%932000\) "South Lebanon conflict (1985–2000)") with [Hezbollah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hezbollah "Hezbollah"). The [First Intifada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Intifada "First Intifada"), a Palestinian uprising against Israeli rule,[^262] broke out in 1987, with waves of uncoordinated demonstrations and violence in the occupied West Bank and Gaza. Over the following six years, the intifada became more organised and included economic and cultural measures aimed at disrupting the Israeli occupation. Over 1,000 people were killed.[^263] During the 1991 [Gulf War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_War "Gulf War"), the PLO supported [Saddam Hussein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saddam_Hussein "Saddam Hussein") and Iraqi missile [attacks against Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraqi_rocket_attacks_on_Israel "Iraqi rocket attacks on Israel"). Despite public outrage, Israel heeded American calls to refrain from hitting back.[^264] [^265]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Foreign_Min._Peres_and_King_Hussein.jpg/250px-Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Foreign_Min._Peres_and_King_Hussein.jpg)

Shimon Peres (left) with Yitzhak Rabin (center) and King Hussein of Jordan (right), prior to signing the Israel–Jordan peace treaty in 1994

In 1992, [Yitzhak Rabin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yitzhak_Rabin "Yitzhak Rabin") became prime minister following [an election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1992_Israeli_legislative_election "1992 Israeli legislative election") in which his party called for compromise with Israel's neighbours.[^266] [^267] The following year, [Shimon Peres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shimon_Peres "Shimon Peres") on behalf of Israel and [Yasser Arafat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yasser_Arafat "Yasser Arafat") for the PLO signed the [Oslo Accords](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oslo_Accords "Oslo Accords"), which gave the [Palestinian National Authority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_Authority "Palestinian Authority") (PNA) the right to govern [parts of the West Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Bank_areas_in_the_Oslo_II_Accord "West Bank areas in the Oslo II Accord") and the Gaza Strip.[^268] The PLO also [recognised Israel's right to exist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Palestine_Liberation_Organization_letters_of_recognition "Israel–Palestine Liberation Organization letters of recognition") and pledged an end to terrorism.[^269] In 1994, the [Israel–Jordan peace treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Jordan_peace_treaty "Israel–Jordan peace treaty") was signed, making Jordan the second Arab country to normalise relations with Israel.[^270] Arab public support for the Accords was damaged by the continuation of Israeli settlements [^271] and [checkpoints](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_checkpoint "Israeli checkpoint"), and the deterioration of economic conditions.[^272] Israeli public support for the Accords waned after [Palestinian suicide attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Palestinian_suicide_attacks "List of Palestinian suicide attacks").[^273] In November 1995, Rabin [was assassinated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Yitzhak_Rabin "Assassination of Yitzhak Rabin") by [Yigal Amir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yigal_Amir "Yigal Amir"), a far-right Jew who opposed the Accords.[^274]

During [Benjamin Netanyahu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu "Benjamin Netanyahu") 's premiership at the end of the 1990s, Israel [agreed to withdraw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protocol_Concerning_the_Redeployment_in_Hebron "Protocol Concerning the Redeployment in Hebron") from [Hebron](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebron "Hebron"),[^275] though this was never ratified or implemented,[^276] and he signed the [Wye River Memorandum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wye_River_Memorandum "Wye River Memorandum"). The agreement dealt with further redeployments in the West Bank and security issues. The memorandum was criticised by major international human rights organisations for its "encouragement" of human rights abuses.[^277] [^278] [Ehud Barak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ehud_Barak "Ehud Barak"), [elected](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999_Israeli_general_election "1999 Israeli general election") prime minister in 1999, withdrew forces from southern Lebanon and conducted negotiations with PNA Chairman Yasser Arafat and U.S. President [Bill Clinton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Clinton "Bill Clinton") at the [2000 Camp David Summit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000_Camp_David_Summit "2000 Camp David Summit"). Barak offered a plan for the establishment of a [Palestinian state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_state "Palestinian state"), including the entirety of the Gaza Strip and over 90% of the West Bank with Jerusalem as a shared capital.[^279] Each side blamed the other for the failure of the talks.

### 21st century

In late 2000, after a controversial visit by Sharon to the [Temple Mount](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temple_Mount "Temple Mount"), the [Second Intifada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Intifada "Second Intifada") began. The popular uprising faced disproportionate repression from the Israeli state.[^280] [Palestinian suicide bombings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_suicide_attacks "Palestinian suicide attacks") eventually developed into a recurrent feature of the intifada.[^281] Some commentators contend that the intifada was pre-planned by Arafat after the collapse of peace talks.[^282] [^283] [^284] [^285] Sharon became prime minister in a [2001 election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001_Israeli_prime_ministerial_election "2001 Israeli prime ministerial election"); he carried out his plan to [unilaterally withdraw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_disengagement_from_the_Gaza_Strip "Israeli disengagement from the Gaza Strip") from the Gaza Strip and spearheaded the construction of the [West Bank barrier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Bank_barrier "West Bank barrier"),[^286] ending the intifada.[^287] Between 2000 and 2008, 1,063 Israelis, 5,517 Palestinians and 64 foreign citizens were killed.[^288]

In July 2006, a Hezbollah artillery assault on Israel's northern border communities and a [cross-border abduction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006_Hezbollah_cross-border_raid "2006 Hezbollah cross-border raid") of two Israeli soldiers precipitated the month-long [Second Lebanon War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006_Lebanon_War "2006 Lebanon War"), including an Israeli invasion of Lebanon.[^289] [^290] The war wound down in August 2006 after the passage of [United Nations Security Council Resolution 1701](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1701 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 1701"); Israeli forces mostly withdrew from Lebanon by October 2006 but continued to occupy the Lebanese portion of [Ghajar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghajar "Ghajar") village.[^291] [^292] In 2007 the Israeli Air Force [destroyed a nuclear reactor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Outside_the_Box "Operation Outside the Box") in Syria.

In 2008, [a ceasefire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_Israel%E2%80%93Hamas_ceasefire "2008 Israel–Hamas ceasefire") between [Hamas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamas "Hamas") and Israel collapsed, resulting in the three-week [Gaza War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_War_\(2008%E2%80%932009\) "Gaza War (2008–2009)").[^293] [^294] In what Israel described as a response to [over a hundred Palestinian rocket attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel_in_2012 "List of Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel in 2012") on southern Israeli cities,[^295] Israel began [an operation in the Gaza Strip](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Gaza_War "2012 Gaza War") in 2012, lasting eight days.[^296] Israel started another [operation in Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Gaza_War "2014 Gaza War") following an escalation of rocket attacks by Hamas in July 2014.[^297] In May 2021, another [round of fighting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Israel%E2%80%93Palestine_crisis "2021 Israel–Palestine crisis") took place in Gaza and Israel, lasting eleven days.[^298] By the 2010s, [increasing regional cooperation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_alliance "Arab–Israeli alliance") between Israel and [Arab League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_League "Arab League") countries have been established, culminating in the signing of the [Abraham Accords](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_Accords "Abraham Accords"). The Israeli security situation shifted from the traditional [Arab–Israeli conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict "Arab–Israeli conflict") towards the [Iran–Israel proxy conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Israel_proxy_conflict "Iran–Israel proxy conflict") and [direct confrontation with Iran during the Syrian civil war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Israel_conflict_during_the_Syrian_civil_war "Iran–Israel conflict during the Syrian civil war").

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Fires_in_Israel_and_the_Gaza_strip_-_7_October_2023_%2853245908850%29.jpg/250px-Fires_in_Israel_and_the_Gaza_strip_-_7_October_2023_%2853245908850%29.jpg)

Satellite view of fires in the Gaza envelope on 7 October 2023

On 7 October 2023, Palestinian militant groups from [Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_Strip "Gaza Strip"), led by Hamas, launched [a series of coordinated attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_7_attacks "October 7 attacks") on Israel, leading to the start of the [Gaza war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_war "Gaza war").[^299] On that day, approximately 1,300 Israelis, predominantly civilians, were killed in communities near the Gaza Strip border and [during a music festival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Re%27im_music_festival_massacre "Re'im music festival massacre").
